                    &hellip;
                    <a href="#"><i class="fa fa-caret-down"></i></a>
                </p>
              </div>

              <p class="j-desc-expand description description-expanded notranslate" itemprop="description">
                Please email hall@coreservlets.com for info on how to arrange customized courses on Java 7, Java 8, JSF 2.2, PrimeFaces, Android, jQuery&#x2F;Ajax, GWT, Hadoop, and other Java EE topics onsite at YOUR location.
<br />
<br />This is the second of two sections on the new Stream interface in Java 8. It covers the Stream methods not already covered in Part 1, most importantly reduce (which is often combined with the earlier map method). It also covers parallel streams and so called &quot;infinite&quot; streams, which are really unbounded-length streams whose values are calculated on the fly. See http:&#x2F;&#x2F;www.coreservlets.com&#x2F;java-8-tutorial&#x2F; for the complete tutorial series (Lambdas and Streams in Java 8) and associated code. That site also lets you download PDF files of each lecture, for saving or printing.  
              </p>
            </div>

        4.
      </a>
    &#xA9; 2015 Marty Hall
Customized Java EE Training: http://courses.coreservlets.com/

reduce: Combining
Stream Elements
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/java-8-streams-part-2-130729180344-phpapp01/95/java-8-tutorial-streams-part-2-map-reduce-parallel-streams-and-infinite-streams-5-638.jpg?cb=1424969307" title="View slide 5 image" target="_blank">
        5.
      </a>
    reduce
&#x2022; Big idea
&#x2013; You start with a seed (identity) value, combine this value with the
first entry of the Stream, combine the result with the second entry of
the Stream, and so forth
&#x2022; Version 1 takes starter value and BinaryOperator. Returns result
directly. Version 2 takes BinaryOperator, with no starter. It starts by
combining first 2 values with each other. Returns an Optional.
&#x2013; reduce is particularly useful when combined with map or filter
&#x2013; Works in parallel if operator is associative and has no side effects
&#x2022; Quick examples
&#x2013; Maximum of numbers
&#x2022; nums.stream().reduce(Double.MIN_VALUE, Double::max)
&#x2013; There is also builtin &#x201C;max&#x201D; method of DoubleStream:
DoubleStream.of(...).max().orElse(Double.MIN_VALUE);
&#x2013; Product of numbers
&#x2022; nums.stream().reduce(1, (n1, n2) -&gt; n1 * n2)
8
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/java-8-streams-part-2-130729180344-phpapp01/95/java-8-tutorial-streams-part-2-map-reduce-parallel-streams-and-infinite-streams-6-638.jpg?cb=1424969307" title="View slide 6 image" target="_blank">
        6.
      </a>
    Concatenating Strings
&#x2022; Code
List&lt;String&gt; letters =
Arrays.asList("a", "b", "c", "d");
String concat = letters.stream()
.reduce("", String::concat);
System.out.printf("Concatenation of %s is %s.%n",
letters, concat);
&#x2022; Results
Concatenation of [a, b, c, d] is abcd.
9
This is the starter (identity) value. It is
combined with the first entry in the Stream.
This is the BinaryOperator. It is the same as
(s1, s2) -&gt; s1 + s2.
It concatenates the seed value with the first Stream
entry, concatenates that resultant String with the
second Stream entry, and so forth.
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/java-8-streams-part-2-130729180344-phpapp01/95/java-8-tutorial-streams-part-2-map-reduce-parallel-streams-and-infinite-streams-7-638.jpg?cb=1424969307" title="View slide 7 image" target="_blank">
        7.
      </a>
    Concatenating Strings:
Variations
&#x2022; Data
&#x2013; List&lt;String&gt; letters = Arrays.asList("a", "b", "c", "d");
&#x2022; Various reductions
&#x2013; letters.stream().reduce("", String::concat);
&#xF0E0; "abcd"
&#x2022; Remember that String::concat here is the same as if you
had written the lambda (s1,s2) -&gt; s1+s2
&#x2013; letters.stream().reduce("", (s1,s2) -&gt; s2+s1);
&#xF0E0; "dcba"
&#x2022; This just reverses the order of the s1 and s2 in the
concatenation
&#x2013; letters.stream().reduce("",
(s1,s2) -&gt; s2.toUpperCase() + s1.toUpperCase());
&#xF0E0; "DCBA"10
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/java-8-streams-part-2-130729180344-phpapp01/95/java-8-tutorial-streams-part-2-map-reduce-parallel-streams-and-infinite-streams-8-638.jpg?cb=1424969307" title="View slide 8 image" target="_blank">
        8.
      </a>
    Finding &#x201C;Biggest&#x201D; Employee
&#x2022; Code
Employee poorest =
new Employee("None", "None", -1, -1);
BinaryOperator&lt;Employee&gt; richer = (e1, e2) -&gt; {
return(e1.getSalary() &gt;= e2.getSalary() ? e1 : e2);
};
Employee richestGoogler =
googlers.stream().reduce(poorest, richer);
System.out.printf("Richest Googler is %s.%n",
richestGoogler);
&#x2022; Results
Richest Googler is Larry Page [Employee#1 $9,999,999].
11
reduce uses the BinaryOperator to combine the starter value with the first Stream entry,
then combines that result with the second Stream entry, and so forth.
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/java-8-streams-part-2-130729180344-phpapp01/95/java-8-tutorial-streams-part-2-map-reduce-parallel-streams-and-infinite-streams-9-638.jpg?cb=1424969307" title="View slide 9 image" target="_blank">
        9.
      </a>
    Finding Biggest Number
&#x2022; Using reduce directly
List&lt;Double&gt; nums1a = Arrays.asList(1.2, -2.3, 4.5, -5.6);
double maxNum1 =
nums1a.stream().reduce(Double.MIN_VALUE, Double::max);
System.out.printf("Max of %s is %s.%n", nums1a, maxNum1);
&#x2022; Using DoubleStream and max
double[] nums1b = {1.2, -2.3, 4.5, -5.6};
double maxNum2 =
DoubleStream.of(nums1b).max()
.orElse(Double.MIN_VALUE);
System.out.printf("Max of [same numbers] is %s.%n",
maxNum2);
&#x2022; Results
Max of [1.2, -2.3, 4.5, -5.6] is 4.5.
Max of [same numbers] is 4.5.
12
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/java-8-streams-part-2-130729180344-phpapp01/95/java-8-tutorial-streams-part-2-map-reduce-parallel-streams-and-infinite-streams-10-638.jpg?cb=1424969307" title="View slide 10 image" target="_blank">
        10.
      </a>
    Summing Numbers:
Three Alternatives
&#x2022; Version 1: same reduce approach as before
List&lt;Integer&gt; nums2 = Arrays.asList(1, 2, 3, 4);
int sum1 = nums2.stream().reduce(0, Integer::sum);
&#x2022; Version 2: using reduce with no starter
&#x2013; Starts by combining first two Stream entries. Since there
might not be 1 or more entries, returns an Optional.
int sum2 =
nums2.stream().reduce(Integer::sum).orElse(0);
&#x2022; Version 3: using sum method of IntStream
&#x2013; Supplying int[] instead of Integer[] to Arrays.stream
results in IntStream. IntStream has builtin sum method.
int[] nums3 = { 1, 2, 3, 4 };
int sum3 = Arrays.stream(nums3).sum();
// Or IntStream.of(nums3).sum()
13
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/java-8-streams-part-2-130729180344-phpapp01/95/java-8-tutorial-streams-part-2-map-reduce-parallel-streams-and-infinite-streams-11-638.jpg?cb=1424969307" title="View slide 11 image" target="_blank">
        11.
      </a>
    Combining map and reduce:
Version 1 (direct reduce)
&#x2022; Code
int sum4 = nums2.stream().map(EmployeeSamples::findGoogler)
.map(Employee::getSalary)
.reduce(0, Integer::sum);
System.out.printf
("Combined salaries of Googlers with IDs %s is $%,d.%n",
nums2, sum4);
&#x2022; Results
Combined salaries of Googlers with IDs [1, 2, 3, 4]
is $33,333,330.

int sum5 = nums2.stream().map(EmployeeSamples::findGoogler)

    &#xA9; 2015 Marty Hall

Operations that Limit
the Stream Size:
limit, skip
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/java-8-streams-part-2-130729180344-phpapp01/95/java-8-tutorial-streams-part-2-map-reduce-parallel-streams-and-infinite-streams-15-638.jpg?cb=1424969307" title="View slide 15 image" target="_blank">
        15.
      </a>
    Limiting Stream Size
&#x2022; Big ideas
&#x2013; limit(n) returns a Stream of the first n elements.
&#x2013; skip(n) returns a Stream starting with element n (i.e., it throws away
the first n elements)
&#x2022; Note: this was called substream in most Java-8 beta releases, and
was renamed to skip quite late. But, skip is better name.
&#x2013; Both are short-circuit operations. E.g., if you have a 1000-element
stream and then do the following, it applies fn1 exactly 10 times,
evaluates pred exactly 10 times, and applies fn2 at most 10 times
strm.map(fn1).filter(pred).map(fn2).limit(10)
&#x2022; Quick examples
&#x2013; First 10 elements
&#x2022; someLongStream.limit(10)
&#x2013; Last 15 elements
&#x2022; twentyElementStream.skip(5)
18
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/java-8-streams-part-2-130729180344-phpapp01/95/java-8-tutorial-streams-part-2-map-reduce-parallel-streams-and-infinite-streams-16-638.jpg?cb=1424969307" title="View slide 16 image" target="_blank">
        16.
      </a>
    limit and skip: Example
&#x2022; Code
List&lt;Employee&gt; googlers = EmployeeSamples.getGooglers();
List&lt;String&gt; emps =
googlers.stream()
.map(Person::getFirstName)
.limit(8)
.skip(2)
.collect(Collectors.toList());
System.out.printf("Names of 6 Googlers: %s.%n", emps);
&#x2022; Point
&#x2013; getFirstName is called only 6 times, even if Stream has
10,000 elements
&#x2022; Results
Names of 6 Googlers:
[Eric, Nikesh, David, Patrick, Susan, Peter].
19
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/java-8-streams-part-2-130729180344-phpapp01/95/java-8-tutorial-streams-part-2-map-reduce-parallel-streams-and-infinite-streams-17-638.jpg?cb=1424969307" title="View slide 17 image" target="_blank">
        17.
      </a>
    &#xA9; 2015 Marty Hall
Customized Java EE Training: http://courses.coreservlets.com/
Java 7, Java 8, JSF 2, PrimeFaces, Android, JSP, Ajax, jQuery, Spring MVC, RESTful Web Services, GWT, Hadoop.

Operations that use
Comparisons: sorted,
min, max, distinct
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/java-8-streams-part-2-130729180344-phpapp01/95/java-8-tutorial-streams-part-2-map-reduce-parallel-streams-and-infinite-streams-18-638.jpg?cb=1424969307" title="View slide 18 image" target="_blank">
        18.
      </a>
    Comparisons
&#x2022; Big ideas
&#x2013; Sorting Streams is more flexible than sorting arrays
because you can do filter and mapping operations first
&#x2013; min and max are more efficient than sorting in forward or
reverse order, then taking first
&#x2013; distinct uses equals as its comparison
&#x2022; Quick examples
&#x2013; Sorting by salary
empStream.map(&#x2026;).filter(&#x2026;).limit(&#x2026;)
.sorted((e1, e2) -&gt; e1.getSalary() - e2.getSalary())
&#x2013; Richest Employee
empStream.max((e1, e2) -&gt; e1.getSalary() &#x2013;
e2.getSalary())
.get();
&#x2013; Words with duplicates removed
stringStream.distinct()
21
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/java-8-streams-part-2-130729180344-phpapp01/95/java-8-tutorial-streams-part-2-map-reduce-parallel-streams-and-infinite-streams-19-638.jpg?cb=1424969307" title="View slide 19 image" target="_blank">
        19.
      </a>
    Sorting
&#x2022; Big ideas
&#x2013; The advantage of someStream.sorted(&#x2026;) over Arrays.sort(&#x2026;)
is that with Streams you can first do operations like map,
filter, limit, skip, and distinct
&#x2013; Doing limit or skip after sorting does not short-circuit in the
same manner as in the previous section
&#x2022; Because the system does not know which are the first or last
elements until after sorting
&#x2013; If the Stream elements implement Comparable, you may omit
the lambda and just use someStream.sorted(). Rare.
&#x2022; Supporting code from Person class
public int firstNameComparer(Person other) {
System.out.println("Comparing first names");
return(firstName.compareTo(other.getFirstName()));
}
22
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/java-8-streams-part-2-130729180344-phpapp01/95/java-8-tutorial-streams-part-2-map-reduce-parallel-streams-and-infinite-streams-20-638.jpg?cb=1424969307" title="View slide 20 image" target="_blank">
        20.
      </a>
    Sorting by Last Name: Example
&#x2022; Code
List&lt;Integer&gt; ids = Arrays.asList(9, 11, 10, 8);
List&lt;Employee&gt; emps1 =
ids.stream().map(EmployeeSamples::findGoogler)
.sorted((e1, e2) -&gt;
e1.getLastName()
.compareTo(e2.getLastName()))
.collect(Collectors.toList());
System.out.printf
("Googlers with ids %s sorted by last name: %s.%n",
ids, emps1);
&#x2022; Results
Googlers with ids [9, 11, 10, 8] sorted by last name:
[Gilad Bracha [Employee#11 $600,000],
Jeffrey Dean [Employee#9 $800,000],
Sanjay Ghemawat [Employee#10 $700,000],
Peter Norvig [Employee#8 $900,000]].
23

  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/java-8-streams-part-2-130729180344-phpapp01/95/java-8-tutorial-streams-part-2-map-reduce-parallel-streams-and-infinite-streams-21-638.jpg?cb=1424969307" title="View slide 21 image" target="_blank">
        21.
      </a>
    Sorting by First Name then
Limiting: Example
&#x2022; Code
List&lt;Employee&gt; emps3 =
sampleEmployees().sorted(Person::firstNameComparer)
.limit(2)
.collect(Collectors.toList());
System.out.printf("Employees sorted by first name: %s.%n",
emps3);
&#x2022; Point
&#x2013; The use of limit(2) does not reduce the number of times
firstNameComparer is called (vs. no limit at all)
&#x2022; Results
Employees sorted by first name:
[Amy Accountant [Employee#25 $85,000],
Archie Architect [Employee#16 $144,444]].

  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/java-8-streams-part-2-130729180344-phpapp01/95/java-8-tutorial-streams-part-2-map-reduce-parallel-streams-and-infinite-streams-22-638.jpg?cb=1424969307" title="View slide 22 image" target="_blank">
        22.
      </a>
    min and max
&#x2022; Big ideas
&#x2013; min and max use the same type of lambdas as sorted,
letting you flexibly find the first or last elements based on
various different criteria
&#x2022; min and max could be easily reproduced by using reduce,
but this is such a common case that the short-hand
reduction methods (min and max) are built in
&#x2013; min and max both return an Optional
&#x2013; Unlike with sorted, you must provide a lambda,
regardless of whether or not the Stream elements
implement Comparable
&#x2022; Performance implications
&#x2013; Using min and max is faster than sorting in forward or
reverse order, then using findFirst
&#x2022; min and max are O(n), sorted is O(n log n)
25
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/java-8-streams-part-2-130729180344-phpapp01/95/java-8-tutorial-streams-part-2-map-reduce-parallel-streams-and-infinite-streams-23-638.jpg?cb=1424969307" title="View slide 23 image" target="_blank">
        23.
      </a>
    min: Example
&#x2022; Code
Employee alphabeticallyFirst =
ids.stream().map(EmployeeSamples::findGoogler)
.min((e1, e2) -&gt;
e1.getLastName()
.compareTo(e2.getLastName()))
.get();
System.out.printf
("Googler from %s with earliest last name: %s.%n",
ids, alphabeticallyFirst);
&#x2022; Results
Googler from [9, 11, 10, 8] with earliest last name:
Gilad Bracha [Employee#11 $600,000].
26
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/java-8-streams-part-2-130729180344-phpapp01/95/java-8-tutorial-streams-part-2-map-reduce-parallel-streams-and-infinite-streams-24-638.jpg?cb=1424969307" title="View slide 24 image" target="_blank">
        24.
      </a>
    max: Example
&#x2022; Code
Employee richest =
ids.stream().map(EmployeeSamples::findGoogler)
.max((e1, e2) -&gt; e1.getSalary() -
e2.getSalary())
.get();
System.out.printf("Richest Googler from %s: %s.%n",
ids, richest);
&#x2022; Results
Richest Googler from [9, 11, 10, 8]:
Peter Norvig [Employee#8 $900,000].

  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/java-8-streams-part-2-130729180344-phpapp01/95/java-8-tutorial-streams-part-2-map-reduce-parallel-streams-and-infinite-streams-25-638.jpg?cb=1424969307" title="View slide 25 image" target="_blank">
        25.

    distinct: Example

List&lt;Integer&gt; ids2 =
Arrays.asList(9, 10, 9, 10, 9, 10);

Operations that Check
Matches:
allMatch, anyMatch,

  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/java-8-streams-part-2-130729180344-phpapp01/95/java-8-tutorial-streams-part-2-map-reduce-parallel-streams-and-infinite-streams-27-638.jpg?cb=1424969307" title="View slide 27 image" target="_blank">
        27.
      </a>
    Checking Matches
&#x2022; Big ideas
&#x2013; allMatch, anyMatch, and noneMatch take a Predicate and
return a boolean. They stop processing once an answer can be
determined.
&#x2022; E.g., if the first element fails the Predicate, allMatch would
immediately return false and skip checking other elements
&#x2013; count simply returns the number of elements
&#x2022; count is a terminal operation, so you cannot first count the
elements, then do a further operation on the same Stream based
on the count
&#x2022; Quick examples
&#x2013; Is there at least one rich dude?
&#x2022; employeeStream.anyMatch(e -&gt; e.getSalary() &gt; 500000)
&#x2013; How many employees match the criteria?
&#x2022; employeeStream.filter(somePredicate).count()
30
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/java-8-streams-part-2-130729180344-phpapp01/95/java-8-tutorial-streams-part-2-map-reduce-parallel-streams-and-infinite-streams-28-638.jpg?cb=1424969307" title="View slide 28 image" target="_blank">
        28.
      </a>
    Matches: Examples
&#x2022; Code
List&lt;Employee&gt; googlers = EmployeeSamples.getGooglers();
boolean isNobodyPoor =
googlers.stream().noneMatch(e -&gt; e.getSalary() &lt; 200000);
Predicate&lt;Employee&gt; megaRich = e -&gt; e.getSalary() &gt; 7000000;
boolean isSomeoneMegaRich = googlers.stream().anyMatch(megaRich);
boolean isEveryoneMegaRich = googlers.stream().allMatch(megaRich);
long numberMegaRich = googlers.stream().filter(megaRich).count();
System.out.printf("Nobody poor? %s.%n", isNobodyPoor);
System.out.printf("Someone mega rich? %s.%n", isSomeoneMegaRich);
System.out.printf("Everyone mega rich? %s.%n", isEveryoneMegaRich);
System.out.printf("Number mega rich: %s.%n", numberMegaRich);
&#x2022; Results
Nobody poor? true.
Someone mega rich? true.
Everyone mega rich? false.
Number mega rich: 3.

Parallel Streams
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/java-8-streams-part-2-130729180344-phpapp01/95/java-8-tutorial-streams-part-2-map-reduce-parallel-streams-and-infinite-streams-30-638.jpg?cb=1424969307" title="View slide 30 image" target="_blank">
        30.
      </a>
    Parallel Streams
&#x2022; Big idea
&#x2013; By designating that a Stream be parallel, the operations
are automatically done in parallel.
&#x2013; No explicit multi-threading code is required.
&#x2022; This is easiest to see with methods like forEach (assuming the
operation is thread-safe!): the performance should scale linearly with
the number of cores. But, even operations like map, filter, reduce, and
findAny can get big performance gains. Operations in those cases must
be stateless and non-interfering (and reduce op must be associative).
&#x2022; Quick examples
&#x2013; Do side effects serially
&#x2022; someStream.forEach(someThreadSafeOp)
&#x2013; Do side effects concurrently
&#x2022; someStream.parallel().forEach(someThreadSafeOp)
33
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/java-8-streams-part-2-130729180344-phpapp01/95/java-8-tutorial-streams-part-2-map-reduce-parallel-streams-and-infinite-streams-31-638.jpg?cb=1424969307" title="View slide 31 image" target="_blank">
        31.
      </a>
    Helper Methods for Timing
private static void timingTest(Stream&lt;Employee&gt; testStream) {
long startTime = System.nanoTime();
testStream.forEach(e -&gt; doSlowOp());
long endTime = System.nanoTime();
System.out.printf(" %.3f seconds.%n",
deltaSeconds(startTime, endTime));
}
private static double deltaSeconds(long startTime,
long endTime) {
return((endTime - startTime) / 1000000000);
}

    Helper Method: Operation that
Takes One Second
// Simulate a time-consuming operation
private static void doSlowOp() {
try {
TimeUnit.SECONDS.sleep(1);
} catch (InterruptedException ie) {
// Nothing to do here.
}
}

    Parallel Example: Code
List&lt;Employee&gt; googlers = EmployeeSamples.getGooglers();
System.out.print("Serial version [11 entries]:");
timingTest(googlers.stream());
int numProcessorsOrCores =
Runtime.getRuntime().availableProcessors();
System.out.printf("Parallel version on %s-core machine:",
numProcessorsOrCores);
timingTest(googlers.stream().parallel());
System.out.print("Serial version [4 entries]:");
timingTest(googlers.stream().limit(4));
System.out.printf("Parallel version on %s-core machine:",
numProcessorsOrCores);
timingTest(googlers.stream().parallel().limit(4));
36
In these examples, you could replace googlers.stream().parallel() with googlers.parallelStream().
But, it is important to know about .parallel(), since parallel() can be done in the middle of a series of
operations, e.g.: someList.stream().filter(&#x2026;).map(&#x2026;).parallel().moreOps(&#x2026;), and parallel() can be
applied to streams created other ways, e.g.: Stream.of(someArray).parallel().ops().

      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/java-8-streams-part-2-130729180344-phpapp01/95/java-8-tutorial-streams-part-2-map-reduce-parallel-streams-and-infinite-streams-35-638.jpg?cb=1424969307" title="View slide 35 image" target="_blank">
        35.
      </a>
    Advantage of Using Streams vs.
Traditional Loops: Parallel Code
&#x2022; Computing sum with normal loop
int[] nums = &#x2026;;
int sum = 0;
for(int num: nums) {
sum += num;
}
&#x2013; Cannot be easily parallelized
&#x2022; Computing sum with reduction operation
int[] nums = &#x2026;;
int sum = IntStream.of(nums).sum();
&#x2013; Can be easily parallelized
int sum2 = IntStream.of(nums).parallel().sum();

  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/java-8-streams-part-2-130729180344-phpapp01/95/java-8-tutorial-streams-part-2-map-reduce-parallel-streams-and-infinite-streams-36-638.jpg?cb=1424969307" title="View slide 36 image" target="_blank">
        36.
      </a>
    Parallel Reduce:
When is it Safe?
&#x2022; Combining operation is associative
&#x2013; I.e., (a op b) op c == a op (b op c)
&#x2022; Determining this is trickier than it looks;
see the exercises where we ask if multiplication
satisfies this requirement
&#x2022; No side effects on global data are performed
&#x2013; Binary operator itself is stateless
&#x2022; Guaranteed if an explicit lambda is used, but not
guaranteed if you directly build an instance of a class that
implements BinaryOperator, or if you use a method
reference that refers to a statefull class.
&#x2013; The operator does not modify global data

Infinite
(Unbounded On-the-Fly)
Streams
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/java-8-streams-part-2-130729180344-phpapp01/95/java-8-tutorial-streams-part-2-map-reduce-parallel-streams-and-infinite-streams-38-638.jpg?cb=1424969307" title="View slide 38 image" target="_blank">
        38.
      </a>
    Infinite Streams: Big Ideas
&#x2022; Stream.generate(valueGenerator)
&#x2013; Stream.generate lets you specify a Supplier. This Supplier is
invoked each time the system needs a Stream element.
&#x2022; Powerful when Supplier maintains state, but won&#x2019;t work in parallel
&#x2022; Stream.iterate(initialValue, valueTransformer)
&#x2013; Stream.iterate lets you specify a seed and a UnaryOperator f. The
seed becomes the first element of the Stream, f(seed) becomes the
second element, f(second) becomes third element, etc.
&#x2022; Usage
&#x2013; The values are not calculated until they are needed
&#x2013; To avoid unterminated processing, you must eventually use a size-
limiting operation like limit or findFirst (but not skip alone)
&#x2022; The point is not really that this is an &#x201C;infinite&#x201D; Stream, but that it is an
unbounded &#x201C;on the fly&#x201D; Stream &#x2013; one with no fixed size, where the
values are calculated as you need them.
41
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/java-8-streams-part-2-130729180344-phpapp01/95/java-8-tutorial-streams-part-2-map-reduce-parallel-streams-and-infinite-streams-39-638.jpg?cb=1424969307" title="View slide 39 image" target="_blank">
        39.
      </a>
    generate
&#x2022; Big ideas
&#x2013; You supply a function (Supplier) to Stream.generate.
Whenever the system needs stream elements, it invokes
the function to get them.
&#x2013; You must limit the Stream size.
&#x2022; Usually with limit. skip alone is not enough, since the size
is still unbounded
&#x2013; The function can maintain state so that new values are
based on any or all of the previous values
&#x2022; Quick example
List&lt;Employee&gt; emps =
Stream.generate(() -&gt; randomEmployee())
.limit(&#x2026;)
.collect(Collectors.toList());

        40.
      </a>

        41.

    Stateful generate Example:
Supplier Code
public class FibonacciMaker implements Supplier&lt;Long&gt; {
private long previous = 0;
private long current = 1;
@Override
public Long get() {
long next = current + previous;
previous = current;
current = next;
return(previous);
}
}
44
Lambdas cannot define instance variables,
so we use a regular class instead of a
lambda to define the Supplier.

public static Stream&lt;Long&gt; makeFibStream() {
return(Stream.generate(new FibonacciMaker()));
}
public static Stream&lt;Long&gt; makeFibStream(int numFibs) {
return(makeFibStream().limit(numFibs));
}
public static List&lt;Long&gt; makeFibList(int numFibs) {
return(makeFibStream(numFibs)
.collect(Collectors.toList()));
}
public static Long[] makeFibArray(int numFibs) {
return(makeFibStream(numFibs).toArray(Long[]::new));
}

    iterate
&#x2022; Big ideas
&#x2013; You specify a seed value and a UnaryOperator f. The
seed becomes the first element of the Stream, f(seed)
becomes the second element, f(second) [i.e., f(f(seed))]
becomes third element, etc.
&#x2013; You must limit the Stream size.
&#x2022; Usually with limit. skip alone is not enough, since the size
is still unbounded
&#x2022; Quick example
List&lt;Integer&gt; powersOfTwo =
Stream.iterate(1, n -&gt; n * 2)
.limit(&#x2026;)
.collect(Collectors.toList());

    More Complex Example:
Large Prime Numbers
&#x2022; Idea
&#x2013; Generate a series of very large consecutive prime
numbers (e.g., 100 or 150 digits or more)
&#x2013; Large primes are used extensively in cryptography
&#x2022; Approach
&#x2013; Start with a prime BigInteger as the seed
&#x2013; Supply a UnaryOperator that finds the first prime number
higher than the given one
&#x2022; Core code
Stream.iterate(Primes.findPrime(numDigits),
Primes::nextPrime)
.limit(someCutoff)

  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/java-8-streams-part-2-130729180344-phpapp01/95/java-8-tutorial-streams-part-2-map-reduce-parallel-streams-and-infinite-streams-48-638.jpg?cb=1424969307" title="View slide 48 image" target="_blank">
        48.
      </a>
    Helper Methods: Idea
&#x2022; Idea
&#x2013; Generate a random odd BigInteger of the requested size,
check if prime, keep adding 2 until you find a match.
&#x2022; Why this is feasible
&#x2013; The BigInteger class has a builtin probabilistic algorithm
(Miller-Rabin test) for determining if a number is prime
without attempting to factor it. It is ultra-fast even for
100-digit or 200-digit numbers.
&#x2013; Technically, there is a 2100 chance that this falsely
identifies a prime, but since 2100 is about the number of
particles in the universe, that&#x2019;s not a very big risk
&#x2022; Algorithm is not fooled by Carmichael numbers
51
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/java-8-streams-part-2-130729180344-phpapp01/95/java-8-tutorial-streams-part-2-map-reduce-parallel-streams-and-infinite-streams-49-638.jpg?cb=1424969307" title="View slide 49 image" target="_blank">
        49.
      </a>
    Helper Methods: Code
public static BigInteger nextPrime(BigInteger start) {
if (isEven(start)) {
start = start.add(ONE);
} else {
start = start.add(TWO);
}
if (start.isProbablePrime(ERR_VAL)) {
return(start);
} else {
return(nextPrime(start));
}
}
public static BigInteger findPrime(int numDigits) {
if (numDigits &lt; 1) {
numDigits = 1;
}
return(nextPrime(randomNum(numDigits)));
}

    Making Stream of Primes
public static Stream&lt;BigInteger&gt; makePrimeStream(int numDigits) {
return(Stream.iterate(Primes.findPrime(numDigits),
Primes::nextPrime));
}
public static Stream&lt;BigInteger&gt; makePrimeStream(int numDigits,
int numPrimes) {
return(makePrimeStream(numDigits).limit(numPrimes));
}
public static List&lt;BigInteger&gt; makePrimeList(int numDigits,
int numPrimes) {
return(makePrimeStream(numDigits, numPrimes).
collect(Collectors.toList()));
}
public static BigInteger[] makePrimeArray(int numDigits, int numPrimes) {
return(makePrimeStream(numDigits, numPrimes).toArray(BigInteger[]::new));
}

Fancier Stream Output

  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/java-8-streams-part-2-130729180344-phpapp01/95/java-8-tutorial-streams-part-2-map-reduce-parallel-streams-and-infinite-streams-53-638.jpg?cb=1424969307" title="View slide 53 image" target="_blank">
        53.
      </a>
    collect
&#x2022; Big idea
&#x2013; Combined with methods in the Collectors class, you can build
many data types out of Streams
&#x2022; Quick examples
&#x2013; List (shown in previous section)
&#x2022; anyStream.collect(toList())
&#x2013; String
&#x2022; stringStream.collect(joining(delimiter)).toString()
&#x2013; Set
&#x2022; anyStream.collect(toSet())
&#x2013; Other collection
&#x2022; anyStream.collect(toCollection(CollectionType::new))
&#x2013; Map
&#x2022; strm.collect(partioningBy(...)), strm.collect(groupingBy(...))
56
For brevity, the examples here assume you have done
&#x201C;import static java.util.stream.Collectors.*&#x201D;,
so that toList() really means Collectors.toList()
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/java-8-streams-part-2-130729180344-phpapp01/95/java-8-tutorial-streams-part-2-map-reduce-parallel-streams-and-infinite-streams-54-638.jpg?cb=1424969307" title="View slide 54 image" target="_blank">
        54.
      </a>
    Building Lists
&#x2022; Code
List&lt;Integer&gt; ids = Arrays.asList(2, 4, 6, 8);
List&lt;Employee&gt; emps =
ids.stream().map(EmployeeSamples::findGoogler)
.collect(Collectors.toList());
System.out.printf("Googlers with ids %s: %s.%n",
ids, emps);
&#x2022; Results
Googlers with ids [2, 4, 6, 8]:
[Sergey Brin [Employee#2 $8,888,888],
Nikesh Arora [Employee#4 $6,666,666],
Patrick Pichette [Employee#6 $4,444,444],
Peter Norvig [Employee#8 $900,000]].
57
Remember that you can do a static import on
java.util.stream.Collectors.* so that you can use toList()
instead of Collectors.toList().
Also recall that List has a builtin toString method that
prints the entries comma-separated inside square brackets.
Here and elsewhere, line breaks and whitespace added to
printouts for readability.
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/java-8-streams-part-2-130729180344-phpapp01/95/java-8-tutorial-streams-part-2-map-reduce-parallel-streams-and-infinite-streams-55-638.jpg?cb=1424969307" title="View slide 55 image" target="_blank">
        55.
      </a>
    Aside: The StringJoiner Class
&#x2022; Big idea
&#x2013; Java 8 added new StringJoiner class that builds delimiter-
separated Strings, with optional prefix and suffix
&#x2013; Java 8 also added static &#x201C;join&#x201D; method to the String class;
it uses StringJoiner
&#x2022; Quick examples (result: "Java, Lisp, Ruby")
&#x2013; Explicit StringJoiner with no prefix or suffix
StringJoiner joiner1 = new StringJoiner(", ");
String result1 =
joiner1.add("Java").add("Lisp").add("Ruby").toString();
&#x2013; Usually easier: String.join convenience method
String result2 = String.join(", ", "Java", "Lisp", "Ruby");
58
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/java-8-streams-part-2-130729180344-phpapp01/95/java-8-tutorial-streams-part-2-map-reduce-parallel-streams-and-infinite-streams-56-638.jpg?cb=1424969307" title="View slide 56 image" target="_blank">
        56.
      </a>
    Building Strings
&#x2022; Code
List&lt;Integer&gt; ids = Arrays.asList(2, 4, 6, 8);
String lastNames =
ids.stream().map(EmployeeSamples::findGoogler)
.map(Employee::getLastName)
.collect(Collectors.joining(", "))
.toString();
System.out.printf("Last names of Googlers with ids %s: %s.%n",
ids, lastNames);
&#x2022; Results
Last names of Googlers with ids [2, 4, 6, 8]:
Brin, Arora, Pichette, Norvig.
59
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/java-8-streams-part-2-130729180344-phpapp01/95/java-8-tutorial-streams-part-2-map-reduce-parallel-streams-and-infinite-streams-57-638.jpg?cb=1424969307" title="View slide 57 image" target="_blank">
        57.
      </a>
    Building Sets
&#x2022; Code
List&lt;Employee&gt; googlers = EmployeeSamples.getGooglers();
Set&lt;String&gt; firstNames =
googlers.stream().map(Employee::getFirstName)
.collect(Collectors.toSet());
Stream.of("Larry", "Harry", "Peter", "Deiter", "Eric", "Barack")
.forEach(s -&gt; System.out.printf
("%s is a Googler? %s.%n",
s,
firstNames.contains(s) ? "Yes" : "No"));
&#x2022; Results
Larry is a Googler? Yes.
Harry is a Googler? No.
Peter is a Googler? Yes.
Deiter is a Googler? No.
Eric is a Googler? Yes.
Barack is a Googler? No.
60
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/java-8-streams-part-2-130729180344-phpapp01/95/java-8-tutorial-streams-part-2-map-reduce-parallel-streams-and-infinite-streams-58-638.jpg?cb=1424969307" title="View slide 58 image" target="_blank">
        58.
      </a>
    Building Other Collections
&#x2022; Big idea
&#x2013; You provide a Supplier&lt;Collection&gt; to collect. Java takes
the resultant Collection and then calls &#x201C;add&#x201D; on each
element of the Stream.
&#x2022; Quick examples
&#x2013; ArrayList
&#x2022; someStream.collect(toCollection(ArrayList::new))
&#x2013; TreeSet
&#x2022; someStream.collect(toCollection(TreeSet::new))
&#x2013; Stack
&#x2022; someStream.collect(toCollection(Stack::new))
&#x2013; Vector
&#x2022; someStream.collect(toCollection(Vector::new))
61
The examples here assume you have done
&#x201C;import static java.util.stream.Collectors.*&#x201D;,
so that toCollection(&#x2026;) really means
Collectors.toCollection(&#x2026;)
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/java-8-streams-part-2-130729180344-phpapp01/95/java-8-tutorial-streams-part-2-map-reduce-parallel-streams-and-infinite-streams-59-638.jpg?cb=1424969307" title="View slide 59 image" target="_blank">
        59.
      </a>
    Building Other Collections:
TreeSet
&#x2022; Code
TreeSet&lt;String&gt; firstNames2 =
googlers.stream()
.map(Employee::getFirstName)
.collect(Collectors.toCollection(TreeSet::new));
Stream.of("Larry", "Harry", "Peter", "Deiter", "Eric", "Barack")
.forEach(s -&gt; System.out.printf
("%s is a Googler? %s.%n",
s,
firstNames2.contains(s) ? "Yes" : "No"));
&#x2022; Results
Larry is a Googler? Yes.
Harry is a Googler? No.
Peter is a Googler? Yes.
Deiter is a Googler? No.
Eric is a Googler? Yes.
Barack is a Googler? No.
62
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/java-8-streams-part-2-130729180344-phpapp01/95/java-8-tutorial-streams-part-2-map-reduce-parallel-streams-and-infinite-streams-60-638.jpg?cb=1424969307" title="View slide 60 image" target="_blank">
        60.
      </a>
    partioningBy: Building Maps
&#x2022; Big idea
&#x2013; You provide a Predicate. It builds a Map where true
maps to a List of entries that passed the Predicate, and
false maps to a List that failed the Predicate.
&#x2022; Quick example
Map&lt;Boolean,List&lt;Employee&gt;&gt; oldTimersMap =
employeeStream().collect
(partitioningBy(e -&gt; e.getEmployeeId() &lt; 10));
&#x2022; Now, oldTimersMap.get(true) returns a List&lt;Employee&gt; of
employees whose ID&#x2019;s are less than 10, and
oldTimersMap.get(false) returns a List&lt;Employee&gt; of
everyone else.
63
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/java-8-streams-part-2-130729180344-phpapp01/95/java-8-tutorial-streams-part-2-map-reduce-parallel-streams-and-infinite-streams-61-638.jpg?cb=1424969307" title="View slide 61 image" target="_blank">
        61.
      </a>
    partitioningBy: Example
&#x2022; Code
Map&lt;Boolean,List&lt;Employee&gt;&gt; richTable =
googlers.stream().collect
(partitioningBy(e -&gt; e.getSalary() &gt; 1000000));
System.out.printf("Googlers with salaries over $1M: %s.%n",
richTable.get(true));
System.out.printf("Destitute Googlers: %s.%n",
richTable.get(false));
&#x2022; Results
Googlers with salaries over $1M: [Larry Page [Employee#1 $9,999,999],
Sergey Brin [Employee#2 $8,888,888], Eric Schmidt [Employee#3 $7,777,777],
Nikesh Arora [Employee#4 $6,666,666], David Drummond [Employee#5 $5,555,555],
Patrick Pichette [Employee#6 $4,444,444],
Susan Wojcicki [Employee#7 $3,333,333]].
Destitute Googlers: [Peter Norvig [Employee#8 $900,000],
Jeffrey Dean [Employee#9 $800,000], Sanjay Ghemawat [Employee#10 $700,000],
Gilad Bracha [Employee#11 $600,000]].
64
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/java-8-streams-part-2-130729180344-phpapp01/95/java-8-tutorial-streams-part-2-map-reduce-parallel-streams-and-infinite-streams-62-638.jpg?cb=1424969307" title="View slide 62 image" target="_blank">
        62.
      </a>
    groupingBy:
Another Way of Building Maps
&#x2022; Big idea
&#x2013; You provide a Function. It builds a Map where each
output value of the Function maps to a List of entries that
gave that value.
&#x2022; E.g., if you supply Employee::getFirstName, it builds a
Map where supplying a first name yields a List of
employees that have that first name.
&#x2022; Quick example
Map&lt;Department,List&lt;Employee&gt;&gt; deptTable =
employeeStream()
.collect(Collectors.groupingBy(Employee::getDepartment));
&#x2022; Now, deptTable.get(someDepartment) returns a List&lt;Employee&gt; of everyone in
that department.
65
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/java-8-streams-part-2-130729180344-phpapp01/95/java-8-tutorial-streams-part-2-map-reduce-parallel-streams-and-infinite-streams-63-638.jpg?cb=1424969307" title="View slide 63 image" target="_blank">
        63.
      </a>
    groupingBy: Supporting Code
&#x2022; Idea
&#x2013; Make a class called Emp that is a simplified Employee
that has a first name, last name, and office/location name,
all as Strings.
&#x2022; Sample Emps
private static Emp[] sampleEmps = {
new Emp("Larry", "Page", "Mountain View"),
new Emp("Sergey", "Brin", "Mountain View"),
new Emp("Lindsay", "Hall", "New York"),
new Emp("Hesky", "Fisher", "New York"),
new Emp("Reto", "Strobl", "Zurich"),
new Emp("Fork", "Guy", "Zurich"),
};
public static List&lt;Emp&gt; getSampleEmps() {
return(Arrays.asList(sampleEmps));
}
66
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/java-8-streams-part-2-130729180344-phpapp01/95/java-8-tutorial-streams-part-2-map-reduce-parallel-streams-and-infinite-streams-64-638.jpg?cb=1424969307" title="View slide 64 image" target="_blank">
        64.
      </a>
    groupingBy: Example
&#x2022; Code
Map&lt;String,List&lt;Emp&gt;&gt; officeTable =
EmpSamples.getSampleEmps().stream()
.collect(Collectors.groupingBy(Emp::getOffice));
System.out.printf("Emps in Mountain View: %s.%n",
officeTable.get("Mountain View"));
System.out.printf("Emps in NY: %s.%n",
officeTable.get("New York"));
System.out.printf("Emps in Zurich: %s.%n",
officeTable.get("Zurich"));
&#x2022; Results
Emps in Mountain View:
[Larry Page [Mountain View], Sergey Brin [Mountain View]].
Emps in NY: [Lindsay Hall [New York], Hesky Fisher [New York]].
Emps in Zurich: [Reto Strobl [Zurich], Fork Guy [Zurich]].
67
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/java-8-streams-part-2-130729180344-phpapp01/95/java-8-tutorial-streams-part-2-map-reduce-parallel-streams-and-infinite-streams-65-638.jpg?cb=1424969307" title="View slide 65 image" target="_blank">
        65.
      </a>
    &#xA9; 2015 Marty Hall
Customized Java EE Training: http://courses.coreservlets.com/
Java 7, Java 8, JSF 2, PrimeFaces, Android, JSP, Ajax, jQuery, Spring MVC, RESTful Web Services, GWT, Hadoop.

Wrap-Up
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/java-8-streams-part-2-130729180344-phpapp01/95/java-8-tutorial-streams-part-2-map-reduce-parallel-streams-and-infinite-streams-66-638.jpg?cb=1424969307" title="View slide 66 image" target="_blank">
        66.
      </a>
    Summary:
More Stream Methods
&#x2022; reduce
&#x2013; someStream.reduce(seedValue, binaryOperator)
&#x2022; Also someStream.reduce(binaryOperator), returning an Optional
&#x2022; Limiting Stream size
&#x2013; limit, skip
&#x2022; Can trigger short-circuiting
&#x2022; Using comparisons
&#x2013; sorted, min, max, distinct
&#x2022; Finding matches
&#x2013; allMatch, anyMatch, noneMatch, count
&#x2022; Fancy output for &#x201C;collect&#x201D;
&#x2013; toList, joining, toSet, toCollection, partioningBy, groupingBy
69
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/java-8-streams-part-2-130729180344-phpapp01/95/java-8-tutorial-streams-part-2-map-reduce-parallel-streams-and-infinite-streams-67-638.jpg?cb=1424969307" title="View slide 67 image" target="_blank">
        67.
      </a>
    Summary:
Fancy Stream Types
&#x2022; Parallel Streams
&#x2013; anyStream.parallel().normalStreamOps(&#x2026;)
&#x2022; Useful also for findAny, map, filter, reduce, etc.
&#x2022; You are responsible for being sure the operations are
threadsafe (especially with forEach operations that modify
shared data) and that the operation for reduce is
associative
&#x2022; Infinite (unbounded on-the-fly) Streams
&#x2013; Stream.generate(someStatelessSupplier).limit(&#x2026;)
&#x2013; Stream.generate(someStatefullSupplier).limit(&#x2026;)
&#x2013; Stream.iterate(seedValue, operatorOnSeed).limit(&#x2026;)
&#x2022; The benefit is that there is no predetermined number of
entries: values are calculated as you need them
70
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/java-8-streams-part-2-130729180344-phpapp01/95/java-8-tutorial-streams-part-2-map-reduce-parallel-streams-and-infinite-streams-68-638.jpg?cb=1424969307" title="View slide 68 image" target="_blank">
        68.
      </a>
    &#xA9; 2015 Marty Hall
Customized Java EE Training: http://courses.coreservlets.com/

              <li class="j-related-item">
  <a data-ssid="41467564"
    data-ssrank="6"
    data-algo-id="21"
    data-score="1"
    class="j-related-impression"
    title="Java 8, Streams &amp; Collectors, patterns, performances and parallelization"
    href="/jpaumard/java-8-streams-collectors-patterns-performances-and-parallelization">

    <div class="related-thumbnail">
      <img class="j-thumbnail j-lazy-thumb"
        alt="Java 8, Streams &amp; Collectors, patterns, performances and parallelization"
        src="//public.slidesharecdn.com/b/images/thumbnail.png"
